Jamison Brereton

61 (670)
Indra
Bharga Prag─Бtha
18 verses: br╠еhat─л alternating with satobr╠еhat─л, arranged in prag─Бthas
This hymn begins with the invitation to soma (vss. 1тАУ3), but the poet soon turns his attention to the gifts Indra will bestow, a theme that dominates the rest of the first half of the hymn (through vs. 8). The sacrificial context returns at this point, and in verses 11тАУ12 the sacrificers seek to harness Indra as their comrade, whose powers they wish to marshal for their protection against hostile forces (see esp. vss. 13, 15тАУ18).
The syntax is fairly straightforward, but there are a number of rare words and hapaxes (e.g., the last two words of vs. 9) and pleasing verbal plays. The poet espe cially likes variable repetition (of the type тАЬunassailable assailantтАЭ vs. 3).

Jamison Brereton Notes

Indra

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay Indra listen to both these our hymns; may the mightiest Maghavan come to us, (plural ased) with ourdevoted offering, to drink the Soma.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Satr─Бcy─Б dhiy─Б = come to us with your wholemind; both our hymns: i.e.whether recited (┼Ы─Бstra) or sung praises (stotra)

Jamison Brereton

If Indra nearby will hear this twofold speech of ours,
the most powerful benefactor will come here to the soma-drinking by reason of our fully focused insight.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The ca in p─Бda a is subordinating, as the accented verb (┼Ыс╣Ыс╣З├бvat) shows.

See Klein DGRV I.245-46.

Geldner, flg. S─Бyaс╣Зa, suggests that the twofold speech (ubh├бyaс╣Г v├бcaс╕е) is Gesang and Vortrag. This is certainly possible, though I wonder if it might be refined to words and melody - that is, not separate performances of songs and recitations, but words set to music - accounting for the grammatical singular.

Griffith

BOTH boons,-may Indra, hitherward turned, listen to this prayer of ours,
And mightiest Maghavan with thought inclined to us come near to drink the Soma juice.

Geldner

Wenn Indra auf diese unsere doppelte Rede herhorchen sollte, so m├╢ge der Gewaltigste, Gabenreiche mit ungeteilter Aufmerksamkeit zum Somatrunk herkommen.

Grassmann

Es h├╢re Indra nahe hier dies unser beiderseit’ges Lied; Der reiche, st├дrkste komme her zum Somatrunk durch das vereinigte Gebet.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHim, self-resplendent, have heaven and earth formed as the showerer, him (they have formed) forstrength; therefore, you sit down first of your peers; your mind loved the Soma.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

For the two Holy Places [=Heaven and Earth] fashioned the bull as sovereign king, for strength.
And as the first among the highest you take your seat, for your mind has desire for soma.

Griffith

For him, strong, independent Ruler, Heaven and Earth have fashioned forth for power and might.
Thou seatest thee as first among thy peers in place, for thy soul longs for Soma juice.

Geldner

Denn diesen Bullen haben beide Welten zum Selbstherrscher, ihn zur Gewalt erschaffen, und als der Erste unter den H├╢chsten nimmst du Platz, denn dein Sinn verlangt nach Soma.

Grassmann

Denn ihn, den starken Selbstgebieter, haben ja zur Kraft die Welten beid’ erzeugt, Und als der h├╢chsten erster setzest du dich hin; denn somaliebend ist dein Sinn.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬIndra, Maghavan of unbroken truth, it ever comes to pass as you in your knowledge may desire, by yourprotection, O handsome-jawed, may we obtain food, speedily, O thunderer, subduing our enemies.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You whose reality cannot be confounded, o bounteous Indra, it will be just as you wish according to your intention.
Might we win the prize with your help, o you of fair lips, as we go quickly, o master of the stones.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On ├бpr─Бmi-satya see Scarlatta 388, inter alia. With him and others (see already Grassmann) I take the first member as derived from pr├б тИЪm─л, but in the common idiom тАШconfoundтАЩ. In my view the compound concerns a regularly expressed anxiety about Indra - does he exist? See, e.g., VIII.100.3 n├йndro ast─л╠Бti n├йma u tva ─Бha тАЬтАШIndra does not exist,тАЩ so says many a one.тАЭ Our compound addresses this by calling him one тАЬwhose reality cannot be confounded.тАЭ GeldnerтАЩs тАЬder sein Versprechen nie brichtтАЭ assumes a meaning тАШpromiseтАЩ for saty├б- that I donтАЩt think is justified for the RV.

ScarlattaтАЩs тАЬdessen Wahrheit unwandelbar istтАЭ is closer to mine, but I donтАЩt think his rendering of the first member is sufficiently pointed.

Griffith

Changeless in truth, O Maghavan Indra, let it be as thou in wisdom willest it.
May we, O fair of check, win booty with thine aid, O Thunderer, swiftly seeking it.

Geldner

Du Freigebiger, der sein Versprechen nie bricht, so soll es geschehen, wie du in deinem Sinne willst, Indra! Durch deinen Beistand m├╢chten wir den Sieg erringen, du Lippenspitzer, indem wir recht bald dazu kommen, Herr des Pre├Яsteins!

Grassmann

O ewig wahrer, m├дchtiger, so soll es sein, wie es dein Sinn, o Indra, will; Wir m├╢gen Gut erlangen, Held, durch deine Gunst in schnellem Lauf, o Schleuderer.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬYou are the increaser of horses, the multiplier of cows; you, deity, with your golden body; none canharm the gifts laid up for me in you; bring me whatever I ask.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

As multiplicity yourself, you are a multiplier of horseflesh, of cattle; you are a golden wellspring, o god,
for no one will shun a gift in your (control). Whatever I beg for, bring that here.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Although paur├б- is generally a PN in the RV (see Mayrhofer, Die Personenname in der с╣Ъgveda-Saс╣Гhit─Б s.v.), reflecting the patronymic it is morphologically, here it cannot be so meant. Among other things, Indra cannot be a descendent of Puru! In this passage it puns on purukс╣Ы╠Бt in the same p─Бda, as well as pur┼лvaso in 3a, pur┼л╠Бin 8a. GeldnerтАЩs tr. takes account of this word play (тАЬMehrer der RossherdeтАЭ), but I donтАЩt think that it should be construed with a genitive as he takes it. I take both genitives (├б┼Ыvasya тАж g├бv─Бm) with purukс╣Ы╠Бt (so also Scarlatta 76) and interpret paur├б- as тАШstemming from / related to much(ness)тАЩ, that is, тАШmuchness itselfтАЩ; тАЬmultiplicity тАж multiplierтАЭ is an attempt to capture the pun in English without undue awkwardness.

In c Geldner (also Oldenberg) takes d─Б╠Бnam as subject: тАЬbei dir bleibt die Gabe niemals aus,тАЭ but the verbal forms to тИЪmс╣Ыdh are otherwise always transitive. Oldenberg cites VII.59.4 as parallel, but the parallelism is only apparent and the verb there is also transitive.

Griffith

Increaser of our steeds and multiplying kine, a golden well, O God, art thou,
For no one may impair the gifts laid up in thee. Bring me whatever thing I ask.

Geldner

Du bist Mehrer der Ro├Яherde, Vermehrer der Rinderherde, ein goldener Born, o Gott, denn bei dir bleibt die Gabe niemals aus. Worum ich dich auch bitte, das bring mit!

Grassmann

Du spendest Rosse, du vermehrst der Rinder Zahl, o Gott, des Goldes Quelle du; Denn nie ersch├╢pfet deiner Gaben F├╝lle sich; was ich auch bitte, bring’ herbei.

Elizarenkova

рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рддреНрд╡рдВ рд╣рд┐ рддреНрд╡рдВ рдЦрд▓реБ ред рд╕рд╛рдорд░реНрдереНрдпрд╛рджреНрджрд╛рддреЗрддрд┐ рдЧрдореНрдпрддреЗ ред рдЕрддрдГ рдПрд╣рд┐ рдЖрдЧрдЪреНрдЫ ред рдЖрдЧрддреНрдп рдЪрд╛рд╕реНрдорднреНрдпрдВ рднрдЧрдВ рднрдЬрдиреАрдпрдВ рдзрдирдВ рд╡рд┐рджрд╛рдГ рд▓рднрд╕реНрд╡ рджрддреНрд╕реНрд╡ ред рдХрд┐рдорд░реНрдердореН ред рд╡рд╕реБрддреНрддрдпреЗ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдВ рд╡рд╕реБрджрд╛рдирд╛рдп ред рд╣реЗ рдордШрд╡рдиреН рдЧрд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрдпреЗ рдЧрд╛ рдЗрдЪреНрдЫрддреЗ рдорд╣реНрдпрдВрдВ рдЙрджреНрд╡рд╡реГрд╖рд╕реНрд╡ рдЙрддреНрд╕рд┐рдЮреНрдЪрд╕реНрд╡ рдЧрд╛рдорд┐рддрд┐ рд╢реЗрд╖рдГ ред рддрдерд╛ рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рдорд┐рд╖реНрдЯрдпреЗ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡реИрд╖рдгрд╡рддреЗ рдорд╣реНрдпрдорд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдЙрддреН рд╡рд╡реГрд╖рд╕реНрд╡ рдЙрддреНрд╕рд┐рдЮреНрдЪрд╕реНрд╡ рджреЗрд╣рд┐ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou are (bounteous), come, may you obtain wealth to distribute to the worshipper; shower your bounty,Maghavan, on me desiring cows, shower it, Indra, on me desiring horses.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Cerave = cetayitre = medh─Бvin, theworshiper

Jamison Brereton

Come on and find fortune, to give goods to the attentive man. Boil up and over, generous one, for the seeking of cattle, up and over for the seeking of horseflesh, Indra.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The two verbs in ab, ├йhi and vid─Б╠Б, seem to conform to the quasi-serial-verb construction (on which see A. Yates 2014 [UCLA IE Conference proceedings]), but h├н makes trouble for this assessment and trouble in general for the interpretation.

Since h├н triggers verb accentuation, the first imperative should be accented eh├н (that is, ─Б + ih├н), not ├йhi (that is, ─Б╠Б+ ihi), as Oldenberg points out. He suggest that ├йhi is parenthetical. This is possible, though ad hoc, but this still leaves the function of h├н in question. It could be interpreted in the mode of Brereton 2012, as marking the first of two imperatives (in this case vid─Б╠Б, if ├йhi is parenthetical) as the basis of the action of the second. Such an interpretation is barely possible here; however, it seems excessively complex, since it requires banishing the truly first imperative ├йhi from structural consideration. My own ad hoc suggestion is that h├н is over-represented in this part of the hymn (2a, 2d, 3c, 5c, 6c) and has been inserted here without its usual function and without triggering verbal accent. But this is of course not a satisfying solution, though it does allow the QSV analysis to be maintained.

For impv. vid─Б╠Бagainst Pp subj. vid─Б╠Бс╕е, see comm. ad IX.19.6. Here the parallel impvs. ├йhi and v─Бvс╣Ыс╣гasva reinforce an impv. interpr.

For the hapax c├йru- see EWA s.v. An association with тИЪci тАШperceiveтАЩ seems possible. Geldner is uncertain, tr. тАШseekingтАЩ, but in n. suggests тАШtravelingтАЩ (to тИЪcar).

Morphologically v─Бvс╣Ыс╣гasva is somewhat problematic: Lubotsky takes it as the medial perfect imperative to a subjunctive stem, K├╝mmel (474) more cautiously as a тАЬthematically builtтАЭ imperative. (It is worth pointing out that a properly built pf. mid.

impv. would come out as *v─Бvс╣Ыkс╣гva and would be multiply ambiguous.

Thematicization would be a good strategy under these circumstances. For further disc. of this set of тАЬthematicтАЭ perfect imperatives see my 2018 тАЬThe Vedic Perfect Imperative and the Status of Modal Forms to Tense-Aspect StemsтАЭ (Fs. Lubotsky) on the perfect imperative.) As is generally noted, this imperative cannot be separated from the medial participle v─Бvс╣Ыс╣г─Бn├б-, which in two of its three occurrences also appears with ├║d. Following Neisser (1893, also Got┼Н 1987), K├╝mmel (474-77) assigns these forms to a root тИЪ2 varс╣г тАШsich ermannen, sich (tatendurstig) erhebenтАЩ (associated with the present varс╣г─Бy├бte, which however appears to be a denominative, not a root formation) separate from тИЪ1 varс╣г тАШregnenтАЩ and translates our passage rather like GeldnerтАЩs тАЬErmannen dichтАжтАЭ I think this separation is unnecessary and also ignores the ─Б╠Б vс╣Ыс╣гasva in 3a. I find the liquid semantics of тИЪvс╣Ыс╣г тАШrainтАЩ not only possible in all the ├║d тИЪvс╣Ыс╣г passages but productive of a striking image: тАШbubble/boil upтАЩ, expressing IndraтАЩs irrespressible excitement and energy.

Griffith

For thou,-come to the worshipper!-wilt find great wealth to make us rich.
Fill thyself full, O Maghavan, for gain of kine, full, Indra, for the gain of steeds.

Geldner

Wohlan, m├╢gest du also f├╝r den Suchenden einen gn├дdigen Herrn ausfindig machen zum Gutschenken! Ermanne dich, Freigebiger, f├╝r den Rinder W├╝nschenden, o Indra, f├╝r den Rosse W├╝nschenden!

Grassmann

So komm denn zu dem opfernden, verleih ihm Gut als reichen Lohn; Ergiesse dich, o reicher, dem der Rinder w├╝nscht, o Indra, und der Rosse w├╝nscht.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬYou grant many hundreds and thousands of herds as a gift (to the offerer), uttering long praises, we,hymning Indra, the destroyer of cities, bring him before us for our protection.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You are ready to give many thousands and hundreds of herds. We of inspired speech have brought the stronghold-splitter here, singing Indra for his help.

Griffith

Thou as thy gift bestowest many hundred herds, yea, many thousands dost thou give.
With singers’ hymns have we brought the Fort-render near, singing to Indra for his grace.

Geldner

Du hast viele tausend und hundert Herden zum Verschenken bereit. Wir haben den Burgenbrecher zur Gnade bewogen mit schwungvollen Worten den Indra besingend.

Grassmann

Du gibst uns viele tausend Heerden zum Geschenk, und gibst uns viele hunderte, Den Burgzerst├╢rer stimmten wir durch weises Lied zur Huld, den Indra durch Gesang.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra, whether it be the unskilled or the skilled who celebrate your praise, each rejoices in his desire foryou, O ┼Ъatakratu, whose wrath presses ever forwards, who meet the foe, proclaiming, “It is I”.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

If without inspiration or if inspired, someone has dedicated his speech to you, Indra,
he will reach elation in devotion to youтАФo you of a hundred resolves, whose battle-fury is upfront, whose (motto is) тАЬI shall win!тАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

Thematically and lexically connected with the preceding verse (8) despite straddling the prag─Бtha boundary. In 8c we identify ourselves as v├нpravacas- тАШhaving inspired speechтАЩ, and in 9ab it is said that either a v├нpra or a non-v├нpra might offer his v├бcas- to Indra, with good results either way. Although this seems like a non-RVic sentiment (esp. after 8c), since ordinarily only good poets (like us) are meant to achieve success, perhaps the тАЬinspired poetтАЭ is being implicitly contrasted with a non-inspired but still skillful poet. In the other occurrence of avipr├б- in the RV (VI.45.2), Indra тАЬplaces vitality even in the uninspired,тАЭ so perhaps, alternatively, here even the uninspired poet achieves success simply by dedicating his product to Indra and acquiring luster by this contact.

The accusative of the offering with тИЪvidh is a bit unusual, but not unprecedented (see, e.g., I.189.1), and GeldnerтАЩs rather deviant tr. тАЬdie Rede recht gemacht hatтАЭ and his alternative suggestion that v├бcaс╕е represents v├бcas─Б at the end of the p─Бda are both unnecessary.

On the apparent bad cadence produced by ├бvidhat, see remarks ad II.1.7, where ArnoldтАЩs suggestion to read a long augment is adopted.

The apparent subj. mamandat certainly can work as a subjunctive in context and is so rendered in the published translation However, note that it immediately precedes t u v─Бy─Б╠Б, beg. with t-, and we might be dealing with an unetymological doubling from an underlying *mamanda tu v─Бy─Б╠Б. The final syllable of the verb would then be light, but this doesnтАЩt cause major metrical problems. Nonetheless, IтАЩm inclined to stick with the subjunctive. On the other hand, on the basis of VII.18.21 and VII.33.1, I now think it is possible that pr├б mamanda(t) should be interpr. as transitive, with тАШyouтАЩ [=Indra] supplied as object, perhaps as haplology from *tv─Б tv─Бy─Б╠Бas I suggest ad VII.18.21. For the motivations for this reinterpr., see disc. there. The altered tr.

would be тАЬтАж will exhilarate / has exhilarated (you) in devotion to you.тАЭ On the other hand, the intrans. interpr. in the published translation makes slightly more sense in this context – and forms of тИЪma(n)d can be either trans. or intrans., so the current tr. could be maintained.

The voc. ahaс╣Гsana is surely rightly explained (Oldenberg ad V.75.2, AiG II.1.327, III.437) as a univerbation of a VP ah├бс╣Г san─Б тАЬI shall winтАЭ (see V.75.2 for another instantiation of this phrase). (AiG II.1.327 suggests ah├бс╣Г saneyam, but the thematic subjunctive matches the compound better.)

Griffith

Whether the simple or the sage, Indra, have offered praise to thee,
He Satakratu! by his love hath gladdened thee, ambitious! ever pressing on!

Geldner

Wenn einer, unberedt oder beredt, dir, Indra, die Rede recht gemacht hat, so sei er deinetwegen sorglos, du Ratreicher, Vorw├дrtseifernder, Gewinns├╝chtiger.

Grassmann

Mag nun das Wort, o Indra, dir Nichtdichter oder Dichter weihn, Wird er dich doch, vielwirkender, dadurch erfreun, vordringender, gewinnender!

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬIf the strong-armed slayer of enemies, the destroyer of cities, will but hear my invocation, we, desiringwealth, will with our praises call one Indra ┼Ъatakratu, the lord of wealth.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

we, seeking goods, will call upon the goods-lord of a hundred resolves, upon Indra, with songs of praise.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner tr. y├бdi as тАШSoтАЩ, which does not seem legitimate to me. It might be possible to read it as *y├бd ─л, even without a following cluster (see Jamison 2002) тАЬwhen he will hear my call,тАЭ but I donтАЩt see that this appreciably improves sense.

Griffith

If he the Strong of arm, the breaker-down of forts, the great Destroyer, hear my call,
We, seeking riches cry to Indra, Lord of wealth, to Satakratu with our lauds.

Geldner

So der starkarmige, zerst├╢rende Burgenbrecher meinen Ruf h├╢ren sollte - wir rufen Sch├дtze begehrend mit Lobliedern Indra, den ratreichen Sch├дtzeherrn.

Falls meinen Ruf der Armgewaltige vernimmt der Burgzerbrecher, der vertilgt, So rufen preisend Indra wir, der vieles wirkt, den G├╝terherrn mit G├╝terlust.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWe are not evil who worship him, nor too poor to offer gifts, nor destitute of sacred fires– sinceassembled together, when the Soma is effused, we make Indra, the showerer, our friend.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

We are not evil:manamahe = to appear, we do not appear eviс╕╖..

Jamison Brereton

Let us not be regarded as evil, or stingy, or greedy,
if just now we will make Indra, the bull, into our companion at the pressing.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Kulikov (339-40, flg. Got┼Н) does not allow a passive reading for medial forms of тИЪman, but aside from Got┼НтАЩs dictum I see nothing against such an interpretation, which fits the passage better than a reflexive one. The hapax ├бr─Бya- is plausibly taken as a negated form derived from the root тИЪr─Б тАШgive, bestowтАЩ by Mayrhofer EWA s.v. ray├н-.

j├бс╕╖hu- (i.e., j├бс╕Нhu-) is also a hapax with no agreed-upon etymology or meaning. Geldner leaves it untr. and Oldenberg simply comments тАЬdunkel.тАЭ See EWA s.v. for references to previous discussions and suggestions. I wonder if it is not related to jaс╣нh├бra- тАШbellyтАЩ, with MIA voicing of intervocalic obstruent between vowels (cf. Pkt.

jaс╕Нhara- тАШbellyтАЩ cited in EWA s.v. jaс╣нh├бra- [though not registered in Turner]), with тАЬbellyтАЭ as the designation of a greedy, voracious person.

The point of the verse seems to be that we donтАЩt want to get a bad reputation for being selfish by grabbing Indra to be our exclusive companion.

Griffith

We count not then as sinners, nor as niggardly or foolish men,
When with the Soma juice which we have shed we make Indra, the Mighty One, our Friend.

Geldner

Nicht halten wir uns f├╝r schlechte Leute noch f├╝r karge, noch f├╝r …., wenn wir jetzt den Bullen Indra zum Genossen beim Soma machen wollen.

Grassmann

Nicht zeigen wir als schlechte uns, als gabenlos und bl├╢den Sinns; Den starken Indra wollen wir beim Somasaft recht zum Genossen machen uns.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWe join (to our rite) the mighty Indra, the subduer of enemies in battles, the inviolate, him to whompraise is due as a debt; he, the best of charioteers, knows (among steeds) the strong racer, and (among men)he, the bounteous (knows) the offerer whom he is to reach.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

We have yoked the strong one, victorious in battles, the undeceivable one who wants what heтАЩs owed.
The winner, the best charioteer recognizes a prizewinning (racehorse), even when itтАЩs a blurтАФwhich is just the one he will attain.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The second member of the hapax compound с╣Ыс╣З├б-k─Бti- belongs with k─Б╠Бmak─Бti- тАШdesiring desiresтАЩ, and I therefore produce a more volition tr. than the usual тАШSchuld forderndтАЩ.

The interpretation of the second hemistich depends on the interpretation of bhс╣Ыm├бm. Grassmann takes it as тАШerrorтАЩ, Geldner as тАШimpatienceтАЩ (Ungeduld), and see EWA s.v. for other suggestions. I consider it a derivative of тИЪbhram тАШwhirlтАЩ, and see it here as qualifying the v─Б╠Бjin-, the prize-winning horse. The point is that a good charioteer recognizes a good horse even when itтАЩs going so fast it becomes a whirling blur. And this fast horse is the one that the knowledgeable charioteer wants and will obtain.

GeldnerтАЩs interpretation is very different: тАЬDer Gewinner тАж versteht die Ungeduld, die den Sieggewohnten erfasst.тАЭ He takes bhс╣Ыm├бm as a noun, the object of v├йd─Б, and the referent of the relative pronoun in d. Since he considers that rel. pronoun the subject of n├б┼Ыat, he must account for acc. y├бm by assuming attraction to v─Бj├нnam from expected nom. *y├бс╕е. My interpretation avoids this unappealing change and also accounts better for the position of the particles ├нd ┼л, since v─Бj├нnam belongs to the main clause not the relative clause, by my reading. Moreover, n├б┼Ыat should be a subjunctive, but his tr. fails to register that.

Him have we yoked in fight, the powerful Conqueror, debt-claimer, not to be deceived.
Best charioteer, the Victor marks each fault, he knows the strong to whom he will come near.

English translation:

тАЬIndra, give us security from him of whom we are afraid, Maghavan, be strong for us with yourprotections; destroy our enemies, destroy those who harm us.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Whatever we are afraid of, Indra, make us unafraid of that.
Bounteous one, exert your ability then through your help for us. Smash away hatreds, away slights.

Jamison Brereton Notes

P─Бda b would literally be тАЬmake lack of fear of that for us,тАЭ which is overly stilted.

P─Бda c reprises 5ab.

Griffith

Indra, give us security from that whereof we are afraid.
Help us, O Maghavan, let thy succour give us this: drive away foes and enemies.

English translation:

тАЬLord of wealth, you are (the bestower) of great wealth and a dwelling plural ce upon your worshipper; assuch, we invoke you, bearing the Soma, O Maghavan, Indra, who are to be honoured with hymns.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

For you, lord of largesse, are (lord) of great largesse and of the dwelling place of him who does honor.
We, who have pressed (the soma), invoke you, bounteous Indra, who long for songs.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Oldenberg takes r─Бdhaspate as a predicated vocative, presumably with at least r─Б╠Бdhaso m├бhaс╕е and possibly kс╣г├бyasya dependent on it. Geldner (whom I follow) supplies a тАЬlordтАЭ for those dependent genitives, which may amount to the same thing.

Griffith

For thou, O liberal Lord of bounty, strengthenest his ample home who worships thee.
So Indra, Maghavan, thou Lover of the Song, we with pressed Soma call on thee,

Geldner

Denn du, Herr der Gabe, bist Herr ├╝ber gro├Яe Gabe, ├╝ber des Verehrers Haus. Dich freigebiger, lobbegehrender Indra, rufen wir bei ausgepre├Яtem Soma.

Grassmann

F├╝r den Verehrer bist du grosser Gaben Herr, und Sch├╝tzer seiner Wohnungen, Drum rufen wir, o reicher, liederfreuter, dich, o Indra, Soma bringend an.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

Jamison Brereton

Indra, spy and Vr╠еtra-smasher, protector from afar, is worth our choosing. He will guard the last one of us and the midmost. Let him protect us from behind and from in front.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The sandhi form ├нndra that opens p─Бda a can be either vocative or nominative. Because of the 3rd ps. verbs of cd, I take it as nominative.

English translation:

тАЬIndra, protect us from the west, from the south, from the north, from the east, protect us from every side;keep far from us supernatural alarm, keep afar the weapons of the demons.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

I.e. protect us from the west, fromthe east, from below, from the north

Jamison Brereton

Protect us from behind, from beneath, from above, from in front, from everywhere, Indra.
Put far away from us fear of the gods, far away the ungodly missiles.

Griffith

Defend us from behind, below, above, in front, on all sides, Indra, shield us well.
Keep far away from us the terror sent from heaven: keep impious weapons far away.

Geldner

Grassmann

Von hinten, unten, oben, vorne sch├╝tze du, von allen Seiten, Indra, uns; Der G├╢tter Schrecken schaffe weit von uns hinweg, der G├╢tterfeinde Lanzen auch.

Elizarenkova

Protect us, Indra, each to-day, each morrow, and each following day.
Our singers, through all days, shalt thou, Lord of the brave, keep safely both by day and night.
